Causality and Created Things
beginner
6 min
Refuting Temporal Precedence in Contingency
The author shows that temporal precedence leads to eternity of bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why interpreting 'preceded by non-existence' as temporal leads to an absurdity, and how the author refutes it by showing it entails the eternity of bodies.

Core Idea
Temporal precedence of non-existence leads to eternal bodies, so the definition fails.

The author now tackles a key misinterpretation. Some thinkers define the contingent as 'preceded by non-existence' without specifying the type of precedence. In this passage, al-Isfahani systematically tests each possible meaning—causal, essential, honorary, spatial, and temporal—and shows that only temporal is problematic, leading to an absurd conclusion. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The author asks: if 'preceded by non-existence' is meant, what type of precedence is intended? He examines each possibility.
This is a critical move in kalam: definitions must be precise.
2
Examine causal and essential precedence
Causal precedence is impossible because non-existence cannot cause existence. Essential precedence is conceded: the contingent's self is prior to its existence from another.
Honorary and spatial are dismissed as obviously not applicable.
3
Focus on temporal precedence
The key case: if non-existence precedes existence temporally, then time must exist. If the precedence has no beginning, time must be eternal.
This is where the argument gets interesting.
4
Follow the chain to absurdity
From natural science, time is a concomitant of motion, which is a concomitant of body. So eternal time implies eternal body. This contradicts the very idea of contingency.
Thus the definition fails if taken temporally.
5
Conclude
The author declares that the interpretation is false because it leads to the eternity of bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن كان المراد بكون العدم سابقاً على وجود التقدم بالعلية فهذا محال : لأن العدم لا يكون علة للوجود . وإن كان المراد به التقدم بالذات، فهذا مسلّم . لأن العالم عندنا ممكن والممكن ليس له من ذاته إلا عدم الإستحقاق ، وله من غيره ثبوت الإستحقاق . وما له من ذاته ، سابق على ما له من غيره ، سبقاً بالذات ، وأما التقدم : بالشرف والمكان، فظاهر الامتناع . بقي التقدم بالزمان فنقول : التقدم بالزمان لا يحصل إلا مع حصول الزمان ، فإذا كان تقدم عدم العالم على وجوده ، تقدماً لا أول له ، وثبت أن هذا التقدم ليس إلا بالزمان ، وثبت التقدم بالزمان لا يحصل إلا مع حصول الزمان ، فهذا يقتضي قدم الزمان . ثم ثبت في الطبيعيات : أن الزمان من لواحق الحركة ، التي هي من لواحق الحسم، فيلزم من قدم الزمان قدم الجسم. فيثبت : أن تفسير حدوث الأجسام بما ذكرتموه يوجب القول بقدم الأجسام ، فكان ما ذكرتموه من التفسير باطلاً .
And if this is established, we say: If what is meant by 'non-existence being prior to existence' is causal precedence, then this is impossible because non-existence cannot be a cause of existence. If what is meant is essential precedence, then this is conceded, because the world in our view is possible (mumkin), and the possible has from itself only non-deservingness (ʿadam al-istiḥqāq), and from other than itself it has the establishment of deservingness. And what it has from itself is prior to what it has from other than itself, by essential precedence. As for honorary and spatial precedence, their impossibility is apparent. What remains is temporal precedence. We say: Temporal precedence does not occur except with the occurrence of time. So if the precedence of the world's non-existence over its existence is a precedence with no beginning, and it is established that this precedence is only temporal, and it is established that temporal precedence does not occur except with the occurrence of time, then this necessitates the eternity of time (qidam al-zamān). Then it is established in the natural sciences (al-ṭabīʿiyyāt) that time is among the concomitants of motion, which is among the concomitants of body. So from the eternity of time follows the eternity of body. Thus it is established that the interpretation of the contingency (ḥudūth) of bodies according to what you have mentioned necessitates the assertion of the eternity of bodies. So what you have mentioned of interpretation is false.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the definition of 'al-hadith' as 'preceded by non-existence' if taken as temporal precedence. The author systematically examines each type of precedence. Causal precedence is impossible because non-existence cannot cause existence. Essential precedence is conceded: the contingent (mumkin) has non-deservingness from itself, so its self is essentially prior to its existence from another. Honorary and spatial are obviously not applicable. The critical case is temporal precedence. The author argues that temporal precedence requires the existence of time. If the non-existence of the world precedes its existence without beginning (i.e., infinite temporal priority), then time must be eternal (qadīm). From natural science, time is a concomitant of motion, which is a concomitant of body. Hence, if time is eternal, body must also be eternal. This leads to the absurd conclusion that bodies are eternal, contradicting the definition of contingency. Thus the definition is false when interpreted temporally.

الوجود

قدم الزمان
قدم الجسم
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'preceded by non-existence' automatically means temporal precedence.
Correction: The author shows that temporal precedence leads to eternal bodies, so the definition must be interpreted otherwise (e.g., essential precedence).

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude if 'preceded by non-existence' is interpreted as temporal precedence?
A) It leads to the eternity of bodies, which is absurd, so the interpretation is false.
B) It leads to the contingency of time, which is acceptable.
C) It leads to the impossibility of motion.
D) It is the only valid interpretation.

Key Takeaway
Interpreting 'preceded by non-existence' as temporal leads to the absurd conclusion that bodies are eternal, so the definition must be understood differently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You acknowledge that from yourself you have only 'adam al-istiḥqāq (non-deservingness of existence). Yet how often do you live as if you deserve something from Allah? Where in your life does entitlement mask the reality of your contingency? Will you consciously remind yourself today that every breath is a gift from Him alone?
?
The author exposes a faulty assumption about time and causality. What faulty assumptions do you hold about the causes of events in your life—perhaps attributing outcomes to mere temporal sequences or secondary causes, forgetting the true Cause? Can you identify one belief today that requires recalibration?
?
If the definition of contingency leads to absurdity when misunderstood, what about your understanding of your own contingency? Have you truly internalized that your existence depends entirely on Allah at every moment, not just at the beginning? What would change in your daily worship if you lived with this awareness?

Refuting 'Preceded by Another Existent'
The author examines the definition 'preceded by another existent' and shows it fails if temporal precedence is intended.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the definition 'preceded by another existent' fails if temporal precedence is intended, and how the other types of precedence are unproblematic.

Core Idea
Temporal precedence of cause over effect implies eternal time, which is absurd.

The author continues to test a second common definition of 'al-muhdath' (the originated): that it is preceded by the existence of another existent. He systematically examines five kinds of precedence to see which one could apply to the cause of the world. Only temporal precedence creates a problem, because it forces time to be eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Familiarize yourself with the flow of the argument.
Notice the five types of precedence listed.
2
Identify the five types of precedence
The author enumerates five types: causal, essential, honorary, spatial, and temporal. Write them down and note the author's judgment on each.
Causal, essential, and honorary are conceded; spatial is false; temporal leads to absurdity.
3
Understand why three types are conceded
The author concedes causal, essential, and honorary precedence because the cause (God) is indeed prior to the world in these ways. This is not controversial.
These precedences do not conflict with the world's possible nature.
4
Examine the spatial case
Spatial precedence is false by agreement, and even if assumed, it does not negate the possibility of eternal worlds. It is irrelevant to the definition.
Spatial priority does not prove the world is originated in time.
5
See why temporal precedence fails
If we take 'preceded' in time, then the cause's priority with no beginning implies time has no beginning, leading to the same absurdity of eternal time and bodies as before.
This repeats the earlier argument against the first definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا فسرتموه بأنه الذي يكون مسبوقاً بوجود غيره ، فنقول : إن أردتم به السبق بالعلية أو بالذات أو بالشرف ، فالكل مسلم . لأن عندنا العالم ممكن لذاته ، واجب الوجوب علته ، فتكون تلك العلة سابقة على العالم بالعلية وبالذات وبالشرف. وأما بالمكان فباطل بالاتفاق، وبتقدير ثبوته، فإنه لا ينافي القول بقدم العالم، لأنه لا يمتنع في أول العقل وجود موجود فوق هذا العالم بالمكان، ويكون دائم الوجود مع دوام هذا العالم. بقي السبق بالزمان فيعود ما ذكرناه من أنه لما كان سابقاً على العالم بالزمان، وكان سبقه على العالم سبقاً لا أول له، فحينئذ يلزم الاعتراف بأن الزمان لا أول لوجوده، وحينئذ يلزم المحال المذكور .
But if you interpret it (al-muhdath) as that which is preceded by the existence of another, we say: If you mean by it causal precedence, or essential precedence, or honorary precedence, then all are conceded. Because in our view the world is possible (mumkin) in itself, and its cause is Necessary of Existence (wājib al-wujūd). So that cause is prior to the world by causal precedence, essential precedence, and honorary precedence. As for spatial precedence, it is false by agreement, and even if it were assumed, it does not negate the assertion of the eternity of the world, because it is not impossible in the first of intellect that there exist an existent spatially above this world, and it is perpetually existent with the perpetuity of this world. What remains is temporal precedence, and then returns what we mentioned: that since it (the cause) was prior to the world in time, and its priority over the world is a priority with no beginning, then it necessitates the admission that time has no beginning to its existence, and then the aforementioned absurdity follows.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage analyzes the definition of 'al-muhdath' as 'preceded by the existence of another existent' (i.e., its cause). The author examines each type of precedence. If intended as causal, essential, or honorary precedence, all are conceded because the cause (God) is prior to the world in these ways. Spatial precedence is false, and even if assumed, it does not conflict with the possibility of an eternal world existing alongside another eternal being. The critical case is again temporal precedence: if the cause is temporally prior to the world with an infinite priority (no beginning), then time itself would have no beginning, leading to the same absurdity of eternal time and bodies as before. Thus this definition also fails if temporal precedence is intended.

Key Terms

السبق بالذات
السبق بالشرف
السبق بالمكان
السبق بالزمان
علة
واجب الوجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any precedence of cause over effect is temporal.
Correction: The author shows that only causal, essential, and honorary precedences are acceptable; temporal precedence leads to absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to the author, which types of precedence are conceded for the cause (God) over the world?
A) Causal, essential, and temporal.
B) Causal, essential, and honorary.
C) Spatial and temporal.
D) Only causal.

Key Takeaway
The definition 'preceded by another existent' only fails if temporal precedence is meant; other precedences are unproblematic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's precedence over creation, do you instinctively imagine a chronological sequence? How does the distinction between temporal and causal precedence challenge that picture? Will you strive to conceive of God as ever-present cause rather than a distant first event?
?
The author argues that temporal precedence of the cause would imply eternal time. Do you ever unconsciously treat time as an absolute, independent container rather than a created thing? How might this lesson correct your perspective and deepen your trust in God's eternal sovereignty?

The Five Types of Precedence and the Impossibility of Causal Precedence
Enumerates five types of precedence and dismisses four.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five distinct meanings of 'precedence' (temporal, causal, essential, honorary, spatial) and why causal precedence is impossible for non-existence.

Core Idea
Non-existence cannot cause existence; essential precedence is conceded.

In this passage, the author refines the discussion by distinguishing five types of precedence. He immediately eliminates causal precedence as impossible, because non-existence cannot be a cause of existence. He then concedes essential precedence, as the contingent world has non-existence inherent to its essence, while honorary and spatial precedence are obviously absurd for non-existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the Arabic passage carefully. Notice how the author lists the types of precedence in a logical order.
Focus on the terms: التقدم بالعلية, التقدم بالذات, التقدم بالشرف, التقدم بالمكان.
2
Identify the five types
List the five types of precedence mentioned: causal, essential, honorary, spatial, and (later) temporal. Understand each definition.
The author dismisses causal, honorary, and spatial; concedes essential; leaves temporal for the next lesson.
3
Understand why causal is impossible
The author says non-existence cannot be a cause of existence. Reflect on the nature of causality: a cause must have some reality.
This is a key point in kalam: non-existence has no causal power.
4
Understand essential precedence
The author concedes essential precedence: the contingent has non-existence from itself, and existence from another. What it has from itself is prior by essence.
This does not prove temporal origination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن كان المراد بكون العدم سابقاً على وجود التقدم بالعلية فهذا محال : لأن العدم لا يكون علة للوجود. وإن كان المراد به التقدم بالذات، فهذا مسلم . لأن العالم عندنا ممكن والممكن ليس له من ذاته إلا عدم الإستحقاق ، وله من غيره ثبوت الإستحقاق . وما له من ذاته ، سابق على ما له من غيره ، سبقاً بالذات ، وأما التقدم بالشرف والمكان، فظاهر الامتناع . بقي التقدم بالزمان فنقول : التقدم بالزمان لا يحصل إلا مع حصول الزمان ، فإذا كان تقدم عدم العالم على وجوده ، تقدماً لا أول له ، وثبت أن هذا التقدم ليس إلا بالزمان ، وثبت التقدم بالزمان لا يحصل إلا مع حصول الزمان ، فهذا يقتضي قدم الزمان . ثم ثبت في الطبيعيات : أن الزمان من لواحق الحركة ، التي هي من لواحق الجسم، فيلزم من قدم الزمان قدم الجسم. فيثبت : أن تفسير حدوث الأجسام بما ذكرتموه يوجب القول بقدم الأجسام ، فكان ما ذكرتموه من التفسير باطلاً.
And if this is established, we say: If what is meant by non-existence preceding existence is causal precedence, that is impossible because non-existence cannot be a cause of existence. And if what is meant by it is essential precedence, this is conceded. For according to us the world is contingent, and the contingent has from itself only non-entitlement, and from other than itself it has entitlement. And what it has from itself is prior to what it has from other than itself, by essential priority. As for precedence in honor and place, impossibility is obvious. There remains temporal precedence. We say: temporal precedence does not occur except with the occurrence of time. So if the precedence of the non-existence of the world over its existence is a precedence with no beginning, and it is established that this precedence is only temporal, and it is established that temporal precedence does not occur except with the occurrence of time, then this necessitates the eternity of time. Then it is established in physics that time is one of the concomitants of motion, which is one of the concomitants of body. So from the eternity of time follows the eternity of body. Thus it is established that the interpretation of the origination of bodies according to what you have mentioned necessitates asserting the eternity of bodies. So what you have mentioned of interpretation is invalid.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that non-existence precedes existence in a temporal sense. The author first examines five possible meanings of 'precedence': causal, essential, honorary, spatial, and temporal. He dismisses causal precedence because non-existence cannot cause existence. He concedes essential precedence, since the world is contingent and non-existence is inherent to its essence. Honorary and spatial precedence are obviously impossible for non-existence. The only remaining possibility is temporal precedence, but the author argues this leads to an absurdity. Temporal precedence requires time, and if the non-existence of the world precedes its existence with no beginning, then time must be eternal. Since time is a concomitant of motion, and motion a concomitant of bodies, the eternity of time implies the eternity of bodies. Thus, the very interpretation intended to prove the world's origination actually entails its eternity. Hence the interpretation is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'precedence' always means temporal precedence, or that all types are plausible for non-existence.
Correction: The author shows there are multiple types, and only essential precedence is plausible, but it does not prove temporal origination.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject causal precedence (التقدم بالعلية) for non-existence?
A) Because non-existence is not a substance
B) Because non-existence cannot be a cause of existence
C) Because causal precedence is the same as essential precedence
D) Because non-existence is eternal

Key Takeaway
The passage clarifies that non-existence cannot have causal, honorary, or spatial precedence over existence; only essential precedence is conceded, but that does not entail temporal origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that from itself, the contingent world has only non-entitlement to existence. Do you live as though your very existence is a gift you do not deserve? In what area of your life do you act entitled to God's blessings? Commit today to thank God for one thing you usually take for granted.
?
Non-existence cannot be a cause of existence. Yet, do you sometimes blame your past failures (non-existences) for your present shortcomings? How does this passage challenge you to stop seeing your past as a cause and instead see God as the only cause of your current state? Write down one negative belief about yourself that you have attributed to your past and replace it with a truth from this lesson.
?
Essential precedence means what you have from yourself (your inherent weakness) is prior to what you have from God. Does your self-image reflect this priority? Are you more aware of your own limitations or of God's provision? Decide today to consciously acknowledge, in a specific situation, that any good in you comes from God alone.

Causality and Created Things

Why Temporal Precedence Leads to the Eternity of Bodies
Refutes temporal precedence by showing it entails eternal time and bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical consequence of interpreting 'non-existence precedes existence' as temporal precedence: it forces the eternity of time and therefore the eternity of bodies, contradicting the intended origination.

Core Idea
Temporal precedence of non-existence requires eternal time, implying eternal bodies.

After dismissing other types, the author now focuses on temporal precedence. He argues that if the non-existence of the world temporally precedes its existence, this precedence has no beginning, which requires time itself to be eternal. Since physics shows that time is a property of motion and motion of bodies, eternal time means eternal bodies. Thus, the very interpretation meant to prove origination actually proves eternity, making the interpretation invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the second Arabic passage
Read the passage from 'بقي التقدم بالزمان' to the end. Follow the logical chain carefully.
Pay attention to the conditional structure: 'إذا...فـ...' (if...then...).
2
Identify the main premise
The author states that temporal precedence only occurs with the existence of time. So if non-existence precedes existence temporally, time must exist.
This is a key link: temporal precedence implies time's reality.
3
Understand the infinite regress
The precedence is said to have no beginning ('لا أول له'), meaning time must be eternal, because it has always existed for this infinite precedence.
The author uses 'قدم الزمان' (eternity of time).
4
Connect to physics
From physics, time is a concomitant of motion, and motion is a concomitant of bodies. Hence eternal time entails eternal bodies.
This is a standard Aristotelian physics assumption used in kalam.
5
Draw the conclusion
Since the interpretation of origination leads to the eternity of bodies, it is self-refuting. Therefore, the claim that non-existence temporally precedes existence is false.
The passage ends with 'فكان ما ذكرتموه من التفسير باطلاً' (so your interpretation is invalid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إن كان المراد بكون العدم سابقاً على وجود التقدم بالعلية فهذا محال : لأن العدم لا يكون علة للوجود. وإن كان المراد به التقدم بالذات، فهذا مسلم . لأن العالم عندنا ممكن والممكن ليس له من ذاته إلا عدم الإستحقاق ، وله من غيره ثبوت الإستحقاق . وما له من ذاته ، سابق على ما له من غيره ، سبقاً بالذات ، وأما التقدم بالشرف والمكان، فظاهر الامتناع . بقي التقدم بالزمان فنقول : التقدم بالزمان لا يحصل إلا مع حصول الزمان ، فإذا كان تقدم عدم العالم على وجوده ، تقدماً لا أول له ، وثبت أن هذا التقدم ليس إلا بالزمان ، وثبت التقدم بالزمان لا يحصل إلا مع حصول الزمان ، فهذا يقتضي قدم الزمان . ثم ثبت في الطبيعيات : أن الزمان من لواحق الحركة ، التي هي من لواحق الجسم، فيلزم من قدم الزمان قدم الجسم. فيثبت : أن تفسير حدوث الأجسام بما ذكرتموه يوجب القول بقدم الأجسام ، فكان ما ذكرتموه من التفسير باطلاً.
And if this is established, we say: If what is meant by non-existence preceding existence is causal precedence, that is impossible because non-existence cannot be a cause of existence. And if what is meant by it is essential precedence, this is conceded. For according to us the world is contingent, and the contingent has from itself only non-entitlement, and from other than itself it has entitlement. And what it has from itself is prior to what it has from other than itself, by essential priority. As for precedence in honor and place, impossibility is obvious. There remains temporal precedence. We say: temporal precedence does not occur except with the occurrence of time. So if the precedence of the non-existence of the world over its existence is a precedence with no beginning, and it is established that this precedence is only temporal, and it is established that temporal precedence does not occur except with the occurrence of time, then this necessitates the eternity of time. Then it is established in physics that time is one of the concomitants of motion, which is one of the concomitants of body. So from the eternity of time follows the eternity of body. Thus it is established that the interpretation of the origination of bodies according to what you have mentioned necessitates asserting the eternity of bodies. So what you have mentioned of interpretation is invalid.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that non-existence precedes existence in a temporal sense. The author first examines five possible meanings of 'precedence': causal, essential, honorary, spatial, and temporal. He dismisses causal precedence because non-existence cannot cause existence. He concedes essential precedence, since the world is contingent and non-existence is inherent to its essence. Honorary and spatial precedence are obviously impossible for non-existence. The only remaining possibility is temporal precedence, but the author argues this leads to an absurdity. Temporal precedence requires time, and if the non-existence of the world precedes its existence with no beginning, then time must be eternal. Since time is a concomitant of motion, and motion a concomitant of bodies, the eternity of time implies the eternity of bodies. Thus, the very interpretation intended to prove the world's origination actually entails its eternity. Hence the interpretation is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that temporal precedence is a straightforward way to prove the world's origination.
Correction: The author shows that this interpretation actually leads to the opposite conclusion—eternity of bodies—making it self-defeating.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude from the argument that temporal precedence leads to eternal time?
A) The world is originated
B) The world is eternal
C) Time is finite
D) Motion is unnecessary

Key Takeaway
The temporal interpretation of 'non-existence precedes existence' is self-refuting because it leads to the eternity of bodies, undermining the claim of origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often speak of God's existence 'before' creation. This lesson shows that if you mean a temporal 'before' with no beginning, you imply eternal time and bodies. Are you comfortable with that implication, or do you need to refine your understanding of God's relationship to time? What steps will you take to ensure your mental model is logically consistent?
?
The author uses premises from physics (time, motion, body) to challenge a theological interpretation. In your own life, do you avoid using reason and observation to examine your core beliefs because you fear contradictions? Will you commit today to trace one of your deeply held beliefs back to its logical foundations, accepting whatever conclusion follows?

intermediate
8 min
Preceded by Another Existence: A Kalam Analysis
Examines the interpretation of 'originated' as preceded by another existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the interpretation of 'originated' as 'preceded by another existence' by distinguishing types of precedence and showing that only temporal precedence leads to absurd consequences.

Core Idea
Not all precedence implies temporal origination.

In this passage, the author considers an alternative definition of 'originated' (al-muhdath): that which is preceded by the existence of another. He systematically examines what type of precedence could be meant and shows that only temporal precedence would support the claim of the world's creation ex nihilo, but that very temporal precedence leads to an infinite regress of time. This careful distinction reveals a key kalam methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Pay attention to the types of precedence listed.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the five types of precedence
Find the five types mentioned: causal, essential, honorific, spatial, temporal. Note the author's ruling for each.
Three are conceded, one is dismissed, one leads to a problem.
3
Understand why three types are conceded
The author concedes causal, essential, and honorific precedence because they apply to the Necessary Existence as cause of the world. They do not imply the world's origination in time.
4
Analyze the dismissal of spatial precedence
Spatial precedence is false by consensus, but even if granted, it does not contradict the eternity of the world because space could be coexistent.
This shows the author's thoroughness.
5
Grasp the dilemma of temporal precedence
If 'preceded by another' means temporal precedence, then since the Necessary Existence's precedence has no beginning, time must be eternal, leading to the same absurdity as before (eternal bodies).
This closes the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما إذا فسرتموه بأنه الذي يكون مسبوقاً بوجود غيره ، فنقول : إن أردتم به السبق بالعلية أو بالذات أو بالشرف ، فالكل مسلم . لأن عندنا العالم ممكن لذاته ، واجب الوجود علته ، فتكون تلك العلة سابقة على العالم بالعلية وبالذات وبالشرف. وأما بالمكان فباطل بالاتفاق، وبتقدير ثبوته، فإنه لا ينافي القول بقدم العالم، لأنه لا يمتنع في أول العقل وجود موجود فوق هذا العالم بالمكان، ويكون دائم الوجود مع دوام هذا العالم بقي السبق بالزمان فيعود ما ذكرناه من أنه لما كان سابقاً على العالم بالزمان، وكان سبقه على العالم سبقاً لا أول له، فحينئذ يلزم الاعتراف بأن الزمان لا أول لوجوده، وحينئذ يلزم المحال المذكور.
But if you interpret it as that which is preceded by the existence of another, we say: If you mean by it precedence in causation or in essence or in honor, all are conceded. For according to us the world is contingent in itself, and the Necessary Existence is its cause. So that cause is prior to the world in causation, in essence, and in honor. As for spatial precedence, it is false by consensus, and if we suppose it, it does not contradict the assertion of the eternity of the world, because it is not impossible in the first intellect that there be an existent above this world in place, and that it be perpetually existent with the perpetuity of this world. There remains temporal precedence, and then what we mentioned returns: that since it was prior to the world in time, and its precedence over the world is a precedence with no beginning, then it is necessary to acknowledge that time has no beginning to its existence, and then the aforementioned impossibility follows.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage continues the analysis by considering an alternative definition of 'originated' (al-muhdath) as 'that which is preceded by the existence of another'. The author distinguishes possible types of precedence. Causal, essential, and honorary precedence are conceded: the Necessary Existence is the cause of the world and is prior in these senses. Spatial precedence is dismissed by consensus, and even if hypothetically granted, it does not imply the world's non-eternity. However, if temporal precedence is intended, the earlier argument applies: a temporal precedence with no beginning necessitates the eternity of time, leading to the same absurdity (eternal bodies). Thus, this interpretation also fails to prove the world's temporal origination without entailing undesirable consequences.

Key Terms

السبق بالعلية
السبق بالذات
السبق بالشرف
السبق بالزمان

Misconception: One might think that 'preceded by another existence' automatically implies temporal origination.
Correction: The author shows that many types of precedence (causal, essential, honorific) do not imply temporal origination. Only temporal precedence would, but it leads to absurd consequences.

Checkpoint

A) Temporal precedence only
B) Causal, essential, and honorific precedence
C) Spatial precedence
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of 'originated' as 'preceded by another existence' fails because only temporal precedence would imply origination, but it leads to the absurdity of eternal time.

?

What practical difference would it make to think of God's action as essential and causal rather than temporal?

The Cause of Time: Free Agent and Sixth Priority
Proves contingency of time, necessity of a free agent, and sixth priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the cause of time must be a free agent and that this establishes a sixth type of priority distinct from the standard five.

Core Idea
The cause of time is a free agent, and its priority is a unique sixth type.

In this passage, the author presents a rigorous argument that time—being contingent and changing—cannot have a necessary cause. Instead, its cause must be a free agent whose priority over time is unlike any of the five standard types. This argument refines our understanding of causality and divine agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the formal logical structure with conditional statements.
2
Understand the contingency of time
The passage starts by stating that the totality of time is possible in itself (mumkin li-dhatihi), which means it needs a cause. Identify this premise and see how it leads to the next step.
This is a standard kalam move: contingent things need an effect.
3
Follow the disproof of a necessitating cause
The author argues that if the cause were a necessitating cause (mujib), then time would be eternal and unchanging, contradicting the very nature of time as something that involves change and succession. Trace this reductio ad absurdum.
This is the core of the proof for free agency.
4
Recognize the free agent and its priority
Once the necessitating cause is ruled out, the cause must be a free agent (mukhtar). A free agent precedes its act, so the agent of time is prior to time itself. That priority cannot be temporal, so it becomes a sixth type of priority distinct from the five standard ones.
This is the conclusion the author was aiming for.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينتج أن مجموع الزمان ممكن لذاته، وكل ممكن لذاته فله مؤثر، فلمجموع الزمان مؤثر، وذلك المؤثر إما موجب أو مختار، والأول باطل. وإلا لدام المعلول بدوام ذات العلة، فكان يلزم أن يكون الزمان موجوداً، مستقر الذات، مبرأ عن التبدل والتلاحق، وكل ما كان كذلك، فهو ليس بزمان، ينتج: أنه لو كان المؤثر في وجود الزمان موجباً بالذات، لزم أن لا يكون الزمان زماناً. وذلك محال. فيثبت: أن المؤثر في الزمان فاعل مختار، والفاعل المختار لا بد وأن يتقدم على فعله. ينتج: أن فاعل الزمان متقدم على وجود الزمان. وذلك التقدم ليس بالزمان وإلا لزم أن يكون الزمان موجوداً، حال عدمه. وذلك محال. فهذا نوع من التقدم، مغاير للتقدم بالزمان، ومغاير لسائر الأقسام المذكورة. وهو المطلوب
It results that the totality of time is possible in itself, and every possible in itself has an effect, so the totality of time has an effect. That effect is either necessitating (mujib) or free (mukhtar). The first is false. Otherwise, the effect would continue as long as the essence of the cause continues, so it would necessarily follow that time is existent, stable in essence, free from change and succession, and everything that is like that is not time. So it follows that if the effect on the existence of time were a necessary cause (mujib bi al-dhat), it would necessarily follow that time would not be time. That is absurd. Thus it is established that the effect on time is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar), and the free agent must precede its act. So it follows that the agent of time is prior to the existence of time. That priority is not temporal; otherwise, time would have to exist while it was non-existent. That is absurd. So this is a kind of priority, distinct from temporal priority and distinct from the other mentioned categories. That is what was sought.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the cause of time must be a free agent and that the priority of that agent over time is a sixth type of priority distinct from the five standard types. The argument begins by asserting that the sum of time is contingent (mumkin li-dhatihi), therefore requiring an efficient cause (mu'aththir). This cause must be either a necessitating cause (mujib) or a free agent (mukhtar). The first option is false: if the cause were necessitating, then because a necessary cause perpetually produces its effect due to its immutable essence, time would be eternal, unchanging, and without succession—contradicting the very definition of time. Hence the cause must be a free agent. A free agent precedes its act, so the agent of time precedes time itself. This priority cannot be temporal, for that would require time to exist before itself. Therefore, this priority is a sixth type, distinct from temporal priority and the other five types mentioned earlier (such as causal, essential, etc.). The passage ends by stating that this is the desired conclusion.

ممكن لذاته
مؤثر
موجب
مختار
فاعل مختار
تقدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the priority of the agent over time is temporal.
Correction: The text explicitly refutes this, establishing it as a distinct sixth type of priority, not temporal.

Checkpoint
Why can't the cause of time be a necessitating cause (mujib)?
A) Because a necessitating cause would make time eternal and unchanging, contradicting the nature of time.
B) Because a necessitating cause cannot create time.
C) Because a necessitating cause would require time to be non-existent.
D) Because a necessitating cause is itself contingent.

Key Takeaway
The cause of time is a free agent, and its priority over time is a sixth type distinct from temporal and other priorities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that if God were a necessitating cause, time would be eternal and unchanging—meaning your life would have no real change or history. Does your daily experience of time as fleeting and changing actually point to God's free will? How does that truth affect your gratitude for each moment?
?
God's priority over time is a unique sixth type that defies human categories. Are you tempted to confine God within your own understanding of 'before' and 'after'? What would it look like to trust that God acts freely outside time, even when you cannot trace His timing?
?
Since time is contingent and its Agent is free, your past, present, and future are not determined by blind necessity. How does knowing that God freely chose to create time and place you within it change the way you approach your next decision? Will you live as if your choices matter to a free and personal Creator?

Third Argument: Time and the Non-Temporal Priority of Non-Existence
Presents a dilemma: whether time is originated or eternal, priority cannot be temporal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the priority of non-existence over existence is not temporal, as shown by a dilemma about time.

Core Idea
Priority is not time-bound — time itself is part of the problem.

This argument tackles the question of whether the 'before' in 'non-existence before existence' is a temporal before. The author presents a powerful dilemma: whether time is created or eternal, the precedence involved cannot be temporal. This forces us to think of priority in a non-temporal way, which is crucial for understanding the relationship between Creator and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the logical flow register.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
Notice the two cases: if time is originated (hadith) and if time is eternal (qadim).
Each horn leads to the conclusion that priority cannot be temporal.
3
Trace the reasoning for each horn
For each case, follow why temporal priority leads to a contradiction and thus cannot hold.
The reasoning relies on the impossibility of time requiring time.
4
Reflect on the concluding question
The argument ends with an analogical question: if non-temporal persistence is conceivable, why not non-temporal origination?
This extends the logic to the main point about the Creator.
5
Connect to the broader purpose
Understand that this argument is part of proving that Allah's existence is not subject to time.
The non-temporal priority is essential for affirming divine precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة: الزمان إما أن يكون حادثاً أو قديماً، فإن كان حادثاً كان عدمه سابقاً على وجوده، وذلك السبق ليس إلا بالزمان، فقد حصل سبق العدم على الوجود من غير حصول الزمان، وإن كان قديماً كان استمراره ليس بالزمان، وإلا لزم افتقار الزمان إلى زمان آخر، وإذا عقل استمرار الشيء لا بسبب الزمان، فلم لا يعقل أيضاً حدوثه لا بسبب الزمان؟
The third argument: Time is either originated (hadith) or eternal (qadim). If it is originated, its non-existence preceded its existence, and that precedence is only by time. So there would be a precedence of non-existence over existence without time occurring. If it is eternal, its persistence is not by time; otherwise, time would need another time. And if the persistence of a thing is conceivable without time, why is its origination also not conceivable without time?
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is the third argument (al-hujja al-thalitha) demonstrating that the priority of non-existence over existence is not temporal. The argument is a dilemma: If time is originated (hadith), then its non-existence precedes its existence. That precedence, if temporal, would require time to exist before time itself, which is impossible. Therefore, precedence must be non-temporal. If time is eternal (qadim), its persistence is not due to time, because if it were, time would need another time, leading to infinite regress. Thus in both cases, priority is not temporal. The argument concludes by inviting the extension: if non-temporal persistence is conceivable, non-temporal origination should also be conceivable.

Key Terms
حادث
قديم
سبق العدم
استمرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is about whether time is created or eternal in itself.
Correction: The argument actually focuses on the nature of priority, using the two possibilities to show that in both cases, the priority cannot be temporal.

Checkpoint
What is the key conclusion of the third argument?
A) Time must be originated.
B) Time must be eternal.
C) The priority of non-existence over existence is not temporal.
D) Time is contingent.

Key Takeaway
The third argument demonstrates that the priority of non-existence over existence is not temporal, using a dilemma about the nature of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This argument strips away any reliance on time as a condition for existence. Does your heart still treat time as a barrier between you and your Creator? How can you begin to live as though His existence is nearer to you than your own jugular vein—right now?
?
The dilemma shows that time itself is contingent. If all your life's plans are built on time, what happens when time fails? Are you building on something that can be annihilated, or on the One who is beyond time?

The Fourth Argument: A Sixth Type of Priority
Establishes a sixth type of priority by analyzing the impossibility of temporal priority among parts of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the priority of non-existence over existence is established as a sixth type, distinct from the five standard categories of priority.

Core Idea
Priority among parts of time cannot be any of the five types, so it must be a sixth type.

This lesson unpacks a dense argument from al-Matalib al-Aliyah. The author begins with an undeniable fact: yesterday is prior to today. He then systematically shows that this priority cannot be due to causality, essence, honor, place, or even time itself — leading to the conclusion that it is a previously unrecognized, sixth type. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the author's innovative position on the priority of non-existence over existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Start by reading the entire Arabic passage and its English translation. Get a sense of the overall flow: observation, elimination of causal priority, then of other types, then of temporal priority, and finally the conclusion of a sixth type.
Pay attention to the two 'faces' and the two 'reasons' — they are the core of the proof.
2
Trace the elimination of causal priority
Identify the two arguments (two 'wajhan') that show yesterday's priority over today cannot be causal. Write them in your own words.
The first uses the similarity of parts of time; the second uses the simultaneity of cause and effect.
3
Understand the temporal priority paradox
The author then shows that even temporal priority among parts of time leads to absurdity. Follow the infinite regress argument and the two specific contradictions.
The key terms are 'zarf' (container) and 'wi'a' (vessel).
4
Connect to the sixth type
Once all five types are eliminated, the priority of parts of time is posited as a sixth type. Reflect on why this matters for the broader argument about the priority of non-existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة: وهو أنه لا شك في أن الأمس متقدم على اليوم، فتقدم الأمس على اليوم ليس بالعلية. ويدل عليه وجهان: الأول: إن أجزاء الزمان متشابهة، فلو كان جزء منها علة للثاني، لزم كون الثاني علة للأول، ولزم كون كل واحد منها علة لنفسه. لما ثبت أن الأشياء المتساوية في الماهية، يجب أن يكون حكمها في اللوازم متساوياً. والثاني: إن العلة واجبة الحصول عند حصول المعلول، فلو كان الجزء الأول من الزمان، علة للجزء الثاني منه، لزم حصولهما معاً. فحينئذ لا يكون الزمان زماناً. هذا خلف. وبهذا الدليل أيضاً ثبت أنه لا يجوز أن يكون تقدم بعض أجزاء الزمان على البعض بالذات أو بالشرف أو بالمكان. بقي أن يكون بالزمان. فنقول هذا أيضاً محال. لأن التقدم بالزمان عبارة عن كون المتقدم حاصلاً في زمان ما كان المتأخر حاصلاً فيه، ثم حصل زمان آخر يحصل فيه ذلك المتأخر، فلو كان بعض أجزاء الزمان متقدماً على البعض بالزمان، لزم أن يكون كل جزء من أجزاء الزمان حاصلا في زمان آخر، بحيث يكون أحدهما ظرفاً للآخر ووعاء له. ثم الكلام في أجزاء ذلك الوعاء كالكلام في الأول، فيلزم أن يكون كل زمان حاصلاً في زمان آخر إلى غير النهاية، وتكون كلها موجودة معاً دفعة واحدة وذلك أيضاً باطل لوجهتين: الأول: إنه يلزم أن لا تكون هذه الساعة الحاضرة ساعة واحدة، بل ساعات غير متناهية، وذلك مدفوع في بديهة العقل. والثاني: إن مجموع الأمسيات الغير المتناهية، متقدم على مجموع الأيام الحاضرة، وتقدم ذلك المجموع على هذا المجموع بالزمان والظرف مغاير للمظروف، فذلك الذي هو ظرف المجموع ووعاؤه، لا بد وأن يكون خارجاً عن ذلك المجموع، لوجب كون الظرف والوعاء مغاير للمظروف، ويجب أن لا يكون خارجاً عنه، لوجوب أن يكون الفرد من أفراد الشيء داخلا في مجموعه، فهذا يقتضي أن يكون الشيء الواحد بالنسبة إلى المجموع الواحد داخلا وخارجاً عنه، وذلك محال. فيثبت بهذا البرهان: أن تقدم بعض أجزاء الزمان على البعض قسم سادس مغاير للأقسام الخمسة، وإذا عقل ذلك فليعقل مثله في تقدم عدم الحادث على وجوده.
The fourth argument: There is no doubt that yesterday is prior to today. So the priority of yesterday over today is not by causality. Two aspects indicate this: First: The parts of time are similar. If one part were the cause of another, then the second would be cause of the first, and each would be cause of itself, because things equal in essence must have equal attributes. Second: The cause is necessarily present when the effect is present. So if the first part of time were the cause of the second, then both would be present together. Then time would not be time. This is a contradiction. By this same argument, it is also established that priority of some parts of time over others cannot be by essence, honor, or place. It remains that it is by time. But we say this is also impossible. Because priority by time means that the prior occurs in a time in which the later was not present, then another time occurs in which the later occurs. So if some parts of time were prior to others by time, then each part would have to occur in another time, such that one is a container (zarf) and vessel (wi'a') for the other. Then the same discussion applies to the parts of that vessel, leading to an infinite regress, and all would exist together simultaneously. This is also invalid for two reasons: First: It implies that this present hour is not one hour but infinite hours, which is rejected by the intellect. Second: The totality of infinite yesterdays is prior to the totality of present days. That priority is by time and container. The container is distinct from the contained. So that which is the container of the totality must be outside the totality, yet it must also be inside because each individual of something is inside its totality. Thus the same thing would be both inside and outside the totality, which is absurd. Thus by this proof it is established that priority of some parts of time over others is a sixth type, distinct from the five types. If that is conceivable, then let a similar thing be conceivable in the priority of non-existence of an originated thing over its existence.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is the fourth argument (al-hujja al-rabi'a) to establish a sixth type of priority for the priority of non-existence over existence. The argument begins with the obvious priority of yesterday over today. It shows that this priority is not causal, because parts of time are similar, so if one caused another, it would lead to circularity and self-causation. Also, cause and effect must be simultaneous, so if one part caused the next, they would coexist, negating temporal sequence. By the same reasoning, priority cannot be by essence, honor, or place. The only remaining possibility is temporal priority. However, temporal priority among parts of time leads to an infinite regress: each part would need to exist in another time, making that time a container for it, and then that container would need its own container, ad infinitum. Moreover, all these times would exist simultaneously, contradicting the nature of time. Two specific absurdities follow: (1) The present hour would be infinitely many hours. (2) The infinite set of past days is prior to the present set; if this priority is temporal, the container of the entire set must be both outside and inside the set—a contradiction. Therefore, priority among parts of time cannot be any of the five types; it is a sixth type. The argument concludes that if this is conceivable, then the priority of non-existence over the existence of an originated thing can be similarly conceived, thereby proving the desired claim.

Key Terms
أجزاء الزمان
علة
ظرف
وعاء
قسم سادس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The priority of parts of time is a form of temporal priority.
Correction: The argument shows that temporal priority among parts of time leads to absurdity, so it cannot be that. It is a sixth type, beyond the five standard categories.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the fourth argument?
A) The parts of time are not contingent.
B) The priority of parts of time is a sixth type of priority.
C) Time is eternal.
D) Yesterday is prior to today by causality.

Key Takeaway
The priority of non-existence over existence is established as a sixth type of priority, distinct from causality, essence, honor, place, and time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The argument demonstrates that the priority of yesterday over today cannot be explained by any of the five categories you rely on daily. In your life, you often assume that one moment causes the next. Can you identify an area where you have mistaken temporal sequence for causality? How will you correct that assumption starting today?
?
Before you existed, your non-existence was prior to your existence in a way that transcends time itself. Does this challenge your sense of self-importance? Will you meditate on the fact that your existence is a gift from God, not a necessary outcome of prior causes?
?
The proof uses the impossibility of an infinite regress to establish a sixth type. Are you living as if your personal history is an infinite chain of causes, or do you acknowledge a first cause beyond time? What change in your worship does this realization demand right now?

The Five Possible Positions on the World's Matter and Form
Classification of five possible positions on the world's matter and form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five logical possibilities regarding whether the world's matter and form are created or eternal, as argued in classical Islamic cosmology.

Core Idea
Only five positions are logically possible regarding the createdness or eternity of the world's matter and form.

Before exploring the arguments for the world's createdness, the author establishes the conceptual grid by which all possible views are mapped. The world is a body composed of matter and form; each can be either eternal or created, giving four clear positions plus a fifth of suspension. This passage sets up the logical space for the ensuing proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the clear logical classification format.
2
Identify the five positions
List the five positions mentioned: both created, both eternal, matter eternal form created, matter created form eternal, suspension of judgment.
The first four are combinations of two binary options (matter and form) each either created or eternal.
3
Reflect on the assumption
The passage assumes the world is composed of matter and form. Why is this assumption important for the classification?
This assumption frames the entire discussion; without it, other positions might be possible.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Understand that this classification clears the ground: the author will later argue for the first position (both created) and refute the others.
This is the introduction to a longer argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن هذا العالم الجسماني المحسوس لا شك أنه جسم موصوف بصفات مخصوصة وذلك الجسم هو المادة وتلك الصفات هي الصورة فنقول العالم إما أن يكون محدثاً بمادته وصورته وإما أن يكون قديماً بمادته وصورته وإما أن يكون قديماً بمادته ومحدثاً بصورته وإما أن يكون محدثاً بمادته وقديماً بصورته وإما أن يتوقف في هذه الأقسام فهذه هي الأقسام الممكنة في هذا الباب.
Know that this physical, sensible world is undoubtedly a body described by specific attributes. That body is the matter, and those attributes are the form. So we say: The world is either created in its matter and form, or eternal in its matter and form, or eternal in its matter and created in its form, or created in its matter and eternal in its form, or one suspends judgment on these divisions. These are the possible divisions in this subject.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage classifies the possible positions regarding the createdness or eternity of the world with respect to its matter (madda) and form (sura). It begins by stating that the world is a body with attributes, where the body is the matter and the attributes are the form. Then it enumerates five logical possibilities: (1) both matter and form are created; (2) both are eternal; (3) matter is eternal but form is created; (4) matter is created but form is eternal; (5) suspension of judgment on the matter. The author emphasizes that these are the only possible divisions in this topic.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the classification is exhaustive but misses the possibility that the world is not composed of matter and form; the author assumes composition.
Correction: The classification is based on the assumption that the world is a body with matter and form. If one rejects that premise, additional positions might be possible, but within the Aristotelian framework used by the author, these five are exhaustive.

Key Takeaway
The author divides all possible views on the world's origin into five exhaustive categories based on whether its matter and form are created or eternal.

?
When you look at the physical world around you, do you instinctively assume it is 'created in both matter and form' because it's what you were taught, or have you personally traced this belief back to its proofs? Which of the five positions does your daily attitude toward the world reflect?
?
The author lists 'suspending judgment' as a legitimate option. Are there aspects of your faith where you have prematurely settled on a position without fully understanding the arguments? What would it cost you to honestly suspend judgment until you have certainty?
?
The classification forces a decision on every person: either the world has a beginning in both its matter and form, or it doesn't. How does this question affect your daily life? Does your belief in the world's createdness change how you treat material possessions and ambitions?

The Third Position: Matter Eternal, Form Created and the Nature of Prime Matter
Presentation of the third position and the internal debate on prime matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third position on the world's eternity, the identification of prime matter as body, and the two main views on bodily identity.

Core Idea
Prime matter is body, but scholars disagree whether bodies differ essentially or only by accidents.

After presenting the first two positions on the world's eternity and temporal creation, the author turns to a third hybrid view: the world is eternal in its underlying matter but created in its specific forms. This position hinges on what that prime matter actually is. The majority identifies it as body, but then a key dispute arises about whether all bodies share the same essence or are fundamentally different.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own classification come through before you interpret.
This passage is a short but dense classification of a theological position and an internal debate.
2
Identify the majority view on prime matter
Notice that the vast majority of scholars say prime matter is body. They define body as a substance capable of different attributes.
3
Distinguish the two subgroups
The majority then splits: some say all bodies are identical in quiddity and differ only by attributes; others say bodies are essentially different, e.g., fire's heat is its essence, earth's cold is its essence.
This dispute has implications for the creation/eternity debate.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how the view on prime matter affects whether the world is considered eternal or created in matter and form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث وهو أن يقال هذا العالم قديم المادة محدث الصورة فهذا البحث مبني على أن المادة الأولى ما هي فقال الجمهور الأعظم من أهل العلم إن المادة الأولى هي الجسم فالجسم ذات قابلة للصفات المختلفة ثم اختلف هؤلاء فمنهم من قال الأجسام متماثلة في تمام الماهية والحقيقة وإنما يخالف بعضها بعضاً بسبب الصفات القائمة بها ومنهم من قال جسم النار مخالف بالماهية لجسم الأرض فحرارة النار عين ذاتها المخصوصة وبرودة الأرض عين ذاتها المخصوصة.
As for the third division—that this world is eternal in matter and created in form—this discussion is based on what the prime matter is. The vast majority of scholars said that the prime matter is body; thus body is a substance capable of different attributes. Then these scholars differed: some said that bodies are identical in their complete quiddity and reality, and they only differ from each other due to the attributes that inhere in them. Others said that the body of fire is different in quiddity from the body of earth; thus the heat of fire is precisely its specific essence, and the cold of earth is precisely its specific essence.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage introduces the third position: the world is eternal in matter but created in form. The key issue is identifying the prime matter (al-madda al-ula). The majority of scholars identify prime matter as body (jism), a substance capable of receiving different attributes. Within this majority, there is a disagreement: the first group holds that all bodies are identical in their complete essence (mahiyya) and reality, differing only by accidents (attributes). The second group holds that bodies are essentially different; for example, fire's heat is its very essence, and earth's cold is its essence, not an accidental attribute.

الجسم
الماهية
الحقيقة

الذات المخصوصة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'prime matter' is something other than body, such as form or the celestial sphere.
Correction: The text explicitly states that the vast majority of scholars identify prime matter as body, a substance capable of attributes.

Checkpoint

C) Prime matter is the celestial sphere
D) Prime matter is the four elements

Key Takeaway
The third position posits an eternal matter created in form, with the majority identifying prime matter as body, but differing on whether bodies are essentially identical or distinct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does your answer affect your awareness of the Creator’s wisdom in assigning distinct properties to each thing?
?
If all bodies were essentially identical and differed only by accidents, what would that imply about the uniqueness and value of each created thing? How would that challenge or reinforce your sense of wonder and gratitude for the specific qualities God has placed in creation?
?
Consider your own body and its attributes—your strength, your senses, your emotions. Are these accidents or essential to who you are? How does this lesson’s debate on quiddity and essence push you to reflect on the nature of your own self and its relationship to the Creator?

Geometric Shapes as Causes of Qualities: Earth and Fire
Subgroup explains heat, cold, etc. as resulting from cubic and tetrahedral shapes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a subgroup of philosophers explained the primary qualities (heat, cold, moisture, dryness) as resulting from specific geometric shapes of bodies.

Core Idea
Heat and cold arise from geometry: cube = density, tetrahedron = penetration.

This passage presents a fascinating attempt to reduce physical qualities to geometric forms. The idea is that the shape of a body determines its behavior and qualities: cubic shapes cause density and coldness, while tetrahedral shapes cause penetration and heat. This theory was part of ancient debates about whether qualities are accidents or essential.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that the passage first refers to the first group (bodies equal in quiddity) and then the subgroup's opinion. Find the descriptions of the cube and tetrahedron.
Pay attention to the causal language: 'إذا كان واقعاً على هذا الشكل امتنع كونه غائصاً' etc.
2
Understand the reasoning for each shape
The text explains why a cube causes density (cannot sink into another) and why a tetrahedron causes burning (penetrates with apex and separates). Grasp the causal link between shape and quality.
Note that the shape itself is said to produce the quality — not an accidental attribute.
3
Reflect on the implications
This view reduces what we perceive as qualities to purely geometric properties. Consider how this differs from viewing qualities as accidents independent of shape.
This is a form of essentialism about geometric structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأولون وهم القائلون بأن الأجسام متساوية في تمام ماهياتها فقد اختلفوا في هذه الصفات التي هي الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة فمنهم من قال إن هذه الصفات عبارة عن وقوع تلك الأجسام على أشكال مخصوصة فالشكل الأرضي هو الذي يحيط به ست مربعات وهو المكعب فإنه إذا كان واقعاً على هذا الشكل امتنع كونه غائصاً في غيره وذلك هو الكثافة والأرضية والشكل الناري هو الذي يحيط به أربع مثلثات متساويات ومتى كان كذلك نفذ في غيره برأسه وإذا نفذ في غيره لزم أن يفرق اتصال ذلك الغير وهذا هو الإحراق والتفريق فكل جسم كان شكله هو المكعب لزم كونه كثيفاً وهو الأرض وكل كان شكله هو هذا الشكل المذكور لزم كونه نفاذاً في غيره ومفرقاً لأجزاء ذلك الغير فيكون محرقاً.
As for the first group—those who say bodies are equal in their complete quiddities—they differed regarding these qualities, which are heat, cold, moisture, and dryness. Among them, some said that these qualities are expressions of the occurrence of those bodies upon specific shapes. The earthly shape is that which is surrounded by six squares, and it is the cube. If it occurs upon this shape, it is prevented from sinking into another, and that is density and earthiness. The fiery shape is that which is surrounded by four equal triangles. Whenever it is like that, it penetrates into another with its apex, and if it penetrates into another, it necessarily separates the connection of that other, and that is burning and separation. So every body whose shape is the cube necessarily becomes dense and it is earth. And every body whose shape is this mentioned shape necessarily becomes penetrating into another and separating the parts of that other, thus it is burning.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage details the view of a subgroup within the first position (bodies identical in essence) who explain the primary qualities (heat, cold, moisture, dryness) as arising from geometric shapes. They give two examples: the earthly shape is a cube (six square faces), which causes density and inability to sink into other bodies, characterizing earth. The fiery shape is a tetrahedron (four equilateral triangles), which causes penetration and separation of other bodies, resulting in burning. Thus, the assignment of qualities to bodies is due to their underlying geometric forms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Heat is an accidental quality that can exist independently of shape.
Correction: This theory argues that heat is not a separate accident but is identical to having a tetrahedral shape; the shape itself produces the effect of burning.

Checkpoint
According to the shape theory, what shape is attributed to earth?
A) Sphere
B) Cube
C) Tetrahedron
D) Octahedron

Key Takeaway
The passage presents a geometric reductionist theory where the shape of a body determines its primary qualities: cube = earth = density, tetrahedron = fire = burning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience physical sensations like cold or heat, do you ever consider that they might be mere outward manifestations of deeper, perhaps geometric, realities? How would your perception of the material world change if you believed that every quality is a sign pointing to a structure ordained by Allah?
?
The passage reduces earth to a cube and fire to a tetrahedron. Have you ever reduced the complexity of Allah's creation to simplistic explanations that leave out His wisdom? What would it mean for you to see the physical world not just as matter but as a lesson in tawheed?
?
This view argues that qualities are not accidental but rooted in shapes. When you sin, do you attribute it to 'accidental' weaknesses, or do you consider the deeper 'shape' of your heart that makes you prone to that sin? How can you reshape your inner self to avoid burning in the Hereafter?

Shape Theory of the Four Qualities
Razi details the shape theory of the four qualities and the geometric shapes assigned to earth, fire, air, and water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how one group of philosophers explained the four qualities (heat, cold, moisture, dryness) as specific geometric shapes of bodies.

Core Idea
The four primary qualities are reducible to shapes: cube for earth, tetrahedron for fire, octahedron for air, icosahedron for water.

This lesson unpacks the first theory presented by Razi: that the four primary qualities are actually the shapes of bodies. The passage describes how each element's shape determines its behavior. We'll examine the geometric assignments and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Context: Bodies equal in essence
Razi begins by reminding us of the first group's position that bodies are identical in essence. They then disagreed about the four qualities. This sets the stage.
2
The shape theory introduced
One subgroup claims the qualities are the occurrence of bodies on specific shapes. Read the Arabic and translation carefully.
3
Earth and fire shapes
Earth is a cube (6 squares) – this prevents it from penetrating others, causing density. Fire is a tetrahedron (4 triangles) – this allows it to penetrate and separate, causing burning.
Notice the causal link between shape and property.
4
Air and water shapes
Air is an octahedron (8 triangles) – quick to change. Water is an icosahedron (20 triangles). The text does not specify the property for water here, but it completes the set.
5
Conclusion of the shape theory
According to this view, the four qualities are just these shapes. Next, Razi presents an alternative.
The alternative view will be covered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأولون وهم القائلون بأن الأجسام متساوية في تمام ماهياتها. فقد اختلفوا في هذه الصفات التي هي الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة . فمنهم من قال : إن هذه الصفات عبارة عن وقوع تلك الأجسام على أشكال مخصوصة . فالشكل الأرضي هو الذي يحيط به ست مربعات . وهو المكعب ، فإنه إذا كان واقعاً على هذا الشكل ، امتنع كونه غائصاً في غيره وذلك هو الكثافة والأرضية . والشكل الناري هو الذي يحيط به أربع مثلثات متساويات ، ومتى كان كذلك ، نفذ في غيره برأسه ، وإذا نفذ في غيره ، لزم أن يفرق اتصال ذلك الغير ، وهذا هو الإحراق والتفريق . فكل جسم كان شكله هو المكعب ، لزم كونه كثيفاً وهو الأرض . وكل كان شكله هو هذا الشكل المذكور ، لزم كونه نفاذاً في غيره ومفرقاً لأجزاء ذلك الغير ، فيكون محرقاً مفرقاً وهو النار ، وكل جسم أحاط به ثمان مثلثات ، كان سريع الإنقلاب من أحاط ضلع إلى ضلع وهو الهواء ، وكل جسم به عشرون مثلثاً فهو الماء . وعلى هذا المذهب فهذه الصفات أعني النارية والمائية والهوائية والأرضية عبارة عن حصول هذه الأشكال المخصوصة . ومن الناس من أنكر ذلك . وزعم : أن هذه الكيفيات الأربعة ، أعني الحرارة والبرودة والرطوبة واليبوسة ، أعراض زائدة على هذه الأشكال مغايرة لها . وهذا هو القول الأظهر
As for the first group, those who say that bodies are equal in their complete essences, they disagreed concerning these attributes which are heat, cold, moisture, and dryness. Among them are those who said: These attributes are expressions of the occurrence of those bodies upon specific shapes. The earthly shape is that which is surrounded by six squares, and it is the cube. When it occurs upon this shape, it is prevented from being immersed in another, and that is density and earthiness. The fiery shape is that which is surrounded by four equal triangles; when it is like that, it penetrates into another with its apex, and when it penetrates into another, it necessarily separates the connection of that other, and that is burning and separation. So every body whose shape is the cube necessarily becomes dense, and it is earth. And every body whose shape is this mentioned shape necessarily becomes penetrating into another and separating the parts of that other, thus being burning and separating, and it is fire. Every body surrounded by eight triangles is quick to change from one side to another, and it is air. Every body with twenty triangles is water. According to this doctrine, these attributes—namely fieriness, wateriness, airiness, and earthiness—are expressions of the occurrence of these specific shapes. And there are some people who denied that and claimed that these four qualities—namely heat, cold, moisture, and dryness—are superadded accidents, additional to these shapes and different from them. And this is the more apparent opinion.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage addresses those who hold that bodies are identical in essence and explains their disagreement regarding the four primary qualities (heat, cold, moisture, dryness). One group argues that these qualities are nothing but the occurrence of specific geometric shapes on bodies. The author details the shapes: earth corresponds to the cube (six squares), fire to a tetrahedron (four triangles), air to an octahedron (eight triangles), and water to an icosahedron (twenty triangles). He then explains how these shapes produce the observed properties: cube prevents penetration (density), tetrahedron penetrates and separates (burning), octahedron is quick to change, and icosahedron is water. According to this view, the qualities are reducible to shapes. Then the author mentions another group that rejects this identification, asserting that these four qualities are superadded accidents distinct from the shapes. The author notes that this latter view is the more apparent (al-azhar) opinion.

الحرارة
البرودة
الرطوبة
اليبوسة
أشكال مخصوصة
المكعب
مثلثات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The four qualities are necessarily shapes.
Correction: Razi presents this as one view, but then offers the alternative that they are superadded accidents, which he considers more apparent.

Checkpoint

B) Tetrahedron (four triangles)
C) Octahedron (eight triangles)

Key Takeaway
The shape theory identifies the four qualities with specific geometric shapes, each responsible for the characteristic behavior of the corresponding element.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The shape theory reduces the qualities of elements to mere geometric forms. When you look at the world around you, do you tend to reduce complex realities to simple explanations? Where in your life might you be oversimplifying things that are actually more nuanced? This week, try to catch yourself in one instance of oversimplification and instead embrace the complexity.
?
Razi presents two views and then indicates which one is more apparent. Are you willing to set aside your initial preferences and adopt the more convincing position even if it is less flashy? Think of a belief you hold strongly that, upon deeper reflection, might not be the most apparent. What would it take for you to change?
?
The shape of earth (cube) makes it dense and unable to immerse. In your spiritual life, is there an area where you are dense – resistant to being penetrated by truth or mercy? What shape has your heart taken, and what would it take for it to become more receptive to divine wisdom?
